    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer4078077658898399068">For fans of Tina Fey and David Sedaris—Internet star Jenny Lawson, aka The Bloggess, makes her literary debut.<br/>  <br/> Jenny Lawson realized that the most mortifying moments of our lives—the ones we’d like to pretend never happened—are in fact the ones that define us. In the #1 <i>New York Times </i>bestseller, <i>Let’s Pretend This Never Happened</i>, Lawson takes readers on a hilarious jour</span>
  <span id="freeText4078077658898399068" style="display:none">For fans of Tina Fey and David Sedaris—Internet star Jenny Lawson, aka The Bloggess, makes her literary debut.<br />  <br /> Jenny Lawson realized that the most mortifying moments of our lives—the ones we’d like to pretend never happened—are in fact the ones that define us. In the #1 <i>New York Times </i>bestseller, <i>Let’s Pretend This Never Happened</i>, Lawson takes readers on a hilarious journey recalling her bizarre upbringing in rural Texas, her devastatingly awkward high school years, and her relationship with her long-suffering husband, Victor. Chapters include: “Stanley the Magical, Talking Squirrel”; “A Series of Angry Post-It Notes to My Husband”; “My Vagina Is Fine. Thanks for Asking”; “And Then I Snuck a Dead Cuban Alligator on an Airplane.” Pictures with captions (no one would believe these things without proof) accompany the text.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/226262-for-crying-out-loud-how-do-i-open-a-book">For crying out loud, how do I open a book to read ?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_226262'><a id="like_count_community_question_226262" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/226262?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">14 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12868761-let-s-pretend-this-never-happened">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/25276499-lexxi-kitty"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1393175162i/25276499._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/25276499-lexxi-kitty">Lexxi Kitty</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">1) Find something that can be used to dry tears. You do not want to mess up the book, now do you?<br/>2) Go to wherever books are sold. I do not know where<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">1) Find something that can be used to dry tears. You do not want to mess up the book, now do you?<br />2) Go to wherever books are sold. I do not know where that might be. Apparently those who do advertisements also do not know. They always leave it to the potential reader to hunt down the books. "Wherever books are sold" is repeated so often in advertisements.<br />3) Once you have acquired a book, carefully lift the cover, trying as best as you can not to cut yourself. Flip through the fifty or so "extra" pages at the front until you find the start of the book. Begin reading. (This step assumes you have a physical book. If you have a nonphysical book, like a digital one, or one made up out of magic, you will need to find a new set of instructions. They likely consist of "turning on the device that can read digital books, selecting that book by clicking the icon/cover for that book, 'flipping' to the start, read; chanting the magical phrase that causes the book to appear and hover in front of you - it may or may not include a demonic like voice reading the book for you, out loud, or might be silent. Be sure to have something that can put out magical fires, as the words are likely to be burning as if on fire).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_353738681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353738681" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2895577-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256984502p2/2895577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353738681?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/2895577-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353738681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4460696262185774854">If you're looking for a Sedaris alternative, this unfortunately isn't it. Which kills me, because I get the feeling Lawson had the potential (and raw material) to knock it out of the park, but it just doesn't come together.<br/><br/>Jenny Lawson is definitely funny. When she really gets going on a story, it's pretty fantastic - but that's only 10% of the book, and the remaining 90% is just awful. I can't help feeling like this book was all written in a single sitting, with little editing or review. It's u</span>
  <span id="freeText4460696262185774854" style="display:none">If you're looking for a Sedaris alternative, this unfortunately isn't it. Which kills me, because I get the feeling Lawson had the potential (and raw material) to knock it out of the park, but it just doesn't come together.<br /><br />Jenny Lawson is definitely funny. When she really gets going on a story, it's pretty fantastic - but that's only 10% of the book, and the remaining 90% is just awful. I can't help feeling like this book was all written in a single sitting, with little editing or review. It's uneven, it's all over the place, and some chapters feel like pure filler - I don't need pages of imaginary post-its written to her husband Victor, for instance. There are lots of places where I think we're just supposed to enjoy Lawson's rapid-fire babble, but it's not babble with meaning to it, it's just nonsense. And that's a shame, because it means the only reason I keep reading is because I'm waiting for another story like the turkeys to show up, and instead I get very tiny moments like the bobcat toss. It's like Lawson forced herself into writing a memoir when she really excels at writing moments. Drawback being, crafting an entire book of curated, arranged moments takes a hell of a lot of concentration and effort, while stream-of-consciousness nonsense is relatively easier.*<br /><br />I could do without the footnotes, which are just irritating - it is hard to explain how badly footnotes work on a Kindle, but between this book and Jasper Fforde I think I could make a compelling case. I could do without the editor's parentheticals (which weirdly are sometimes also footnotes). I could do without the long-winded flourishes that loop back in on themselves when talking about absolute rubbish. <br /><br />And that all sucks, because Lawson's childhood sounds enjoyably nuts. When she actually stitches a story together, one with multiple events and a timeline, it's HILARIOUS. But all too often, she's just throwing the punchline in there without much else. <br /><br />In the end, I guess this is where I end up with LPTNH: weird shit happens to everyone, but few people know how to structure the story in a way that legitimately entertains. Lawson knows how to structure a story, she's just not choosing to do it most of the time. Also, people are very capable of acting like crazy insane people quite frequently - if you sound too pleased with how wild and crazy you are and keep thumping on about it, it can get REALLY ANNOYING.<br /><br />* I do recognize that Lawson also writes about her general anxiety disorder, and she explains that she finds herself almost incoherent in social situations and is much better on email, when she can edit. But given that this is a book, it feels like a lot of the narrative flailing could have been avoided through editing. We definitely get a good grasp of what it's like to be inside Lawson's head, but she finds her condition exhausting and for a whole book, so did I. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4460696262185774854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_864638712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864638712" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/864638712?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611760859" href="/book/show/12844430-let-s-pretend-this-never-happened">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864638712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2318592830216781461">First, I should mention that I listened to this one on audiobook. Didn't read the text version. <br/><br/>Second, the audio version is read by the author. I think Jenny did a nice job with it, too. If you're used to nothing but professional audiobook narrators, there might be a few verbal ticks in here that might bug you. But me? For an autobiographical work like this? I'd much rather hear it in the author's own voice. <br/><br/>Third, she got some actual laughs out of me. Not just amusement or smiles. Not just chu</span>
  <span id="freeText2318592830216781461" style="display:none">First, I should mention that I listened to this one on audiobook. Didn't read the text version. <br /><br />Second, the audio version is read by the author. I think Jenny did a nice job with it, too. If you're used to nothing but professional audiobook narrators, there might be a few verbal ticks in here that might bug you. But me? For an autobiographical work like this? I'd much rather hear it in the author's own voice. <br /><br />Third, she got some actual laughs out of me. Not just amusement or smiles. Not just chuckles. Real laughs. I was driving around in my car, alone, laughing like a madman. <br /><br />Fourth, several times I sat in the car after I'd finished whatever trip I was taking just to continue listening to the audiobook. <br /><br />Fifth, driving around, listening to this audiobook, I missed the proper turnoff several times. I didn't mind much, because turning around and driving back the right way gave me more time to listen to the book. <br /><br />Sixth, she made me cry reading this. Three times. Now admittedly, I seem to be rather soppy lately. But even given my recent emotional fragility, that's a mark of good writing some good writing. <br /><br />Seventh, the stories Jenny Lawson tells are, in turns: crushingly honest, funny, witty, sweet, heartbreaking, and delightfully bizarre. <br /><br />Lastly, I'd like to say that while I've read some of Jenny's blog, and I know of her considerably fame as The Bloggess, I didn't pick this book up because I was a fan. I bought this audiobook audio because I like her, and I've heard people say good things about it. <br /><br />After listening to it? Yeah. Now I'm a fan. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2318592830216781461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2625110198" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2625110198?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=baddaybooks">baddaybooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2625110198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3237234695700182679"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Need a good read for a bad day? Here's a <u><b><a href='https://youtu.be/-GuEMAaGS3I' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booktube Video</a></b></u> with nine fabulous suggestions!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576431479i/28616836._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote><br/><br/><i>In short? It is exhausting being me.</i>Jenny Lawson (the Bloggess) has <b>lit up the literary scene </b>with her debut novel - Let's Pretend This Never Happened.<br/><br/>Jenny lives the sort of life where... well... hmm... maybe you will just have to <b>read this book yourself. </b><br/><br/>I really don't think I have anything that can adequately sum this one up...<br/><br/>Let's just say if you are<b> a fan of taxidermied animals,</b> </span>
  <span id="freeText3237234695700182679" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605371177i/30377107._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Need a good read for a bad day? Here's a <u><b><a href="https://youtu.be/-GuEMAaGS3I" rel="nofollow noopener">Booktube Video</a></b></u> with nine fabulous suggestions!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576431479i/28616836._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><br><br><i>In short? It is exhausting being me.</i>Jenny Lawson (the Bloggess) has <b>lit up the literary scene </b>with her debut novel - Let's Pretend This Never Happened.<br><br>Jenny lives the sort of life where... well... hmm... maybe you will just have to <b>read this book yourself. </b><br><br>I really don't think I have anything that can adequately sum this one up...<br><br>Let's just say if you are<b> a fan of taxidermied animals,</b> heavily awkward moments, vindictive post-it note wars, crippling anxiety and frank talks about bodily functions, then this book is for you.<blockquote>
  <i>A friend is someone who knows where all your bodies are buried. Because they're the ones who helped you put them there.</i>
</blockquote><b>And the humor! </b><br><br>Oh there is no way to adequately convey Jenny's source of humor - it was just absolutely perfect for me. Really knocked it out of the park!<br><br>I really enjoyed Jenny's take on the world.<br><br>She has had her fair share of heart-stopping, heart-wrenching and <b>jaw-dropping moments</b> ...and yet, when she reflects on them, she says:<blockquote>
  <i>
    
  </i>
</blockquote>And I appreciated her frank talk about mental illness. I feel like that is a subject all too easily (and too often) glossed over in books. It's refreshing (and truly wonderful) to have a book that does not hold back.<blockquote>
  <i>One moment I'm perfectly fine and the next I feel a wave of nausea, then panic. Then I can't catch my breath and I know I'm about to lose control and all I want to do is escape. Except that the one thing I can't escape from is the very thing I want to run away from... me.</i>
</blockquote><b>All in all, I really couldn't have enjoyed this book more. </b><br><br>Every note was just perfectly done - I adored it from cover to cover.<blockquote>
  <i>Knock-knock, motherfucker.</i>

<div id="review_631210557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/631210557" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/631210557?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer631210557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14141493240499502498"><b>JENNY LAWSON ATTACKED ME WITH A MACHETE!!</b><br/><br/>OK, so I have never met Jenny Lawson, and she didn't attack me with an <i>actual</i> machete, but I'm being metaphorical here, y'all.<br/><br/>Because reading Jenny Lawson's book made me feel as if I were being beaten with some kind of weapon, and it may as well have been a machete. Which is a word she uses in her book. She also likes the words chupacabra and vagina. And numerous swear words. She also likes postscripts. Lots of them.<br/><br/>But back to the machete. I opened my re</span>
  <span id="freeText14141493240499502498" style="display:none"><b>JENNY LAWSON ATTACKED ME WITH A MACHETE!!</b><br /><br />OK, so I have never met Jenny Lawson, and she didn't attack me with an <i>actual</i> machete, but I'm being metaphorical here, y'all.<br /><br />Because reading Jenny Lawson's book made me feel as if I were being beaten with some kind of weapon, and it may as well have been a machete. Which is a word she uses in her book. She also likes the words chupacabra and vagina. And numerous swear words. She also likes postscripts. Lots of them.<br /><br />But back to the machete. I opened my review this way to demonstrate how Jenny has written her memoir. She will say something totally exaggerated and in a hysterical voice, and then she tells a 30-minute story, after which you realize the thing that actually happened has nothing to do with what she <i>claimed</i> happened.<br /><br />For example, when Jenny says: "I was attacked by a bear last night!" What she really means is: "I saw a stray cat by the pool."<br /><br />When Jenny says: "I was mauled by a pack of wild dogs!" What she means is: "The neighbor's pet was excited to see me."<br /><br />When Jenny says: "I was stabbed in the face by a serial killer!" She means: "The cat sat on my head while I was asleep."<br /><br />Halfway through the book, I realized Jenny Lawson is a fabulist and a narcissist.<br /><br />Put another way, Jenny Lawson is a very successful blogger. I think the terms have become interchangeable.<br /><br />Here is a quote from one of Jenny's chapters, in which she shares ridiculous and inappropriate emails to a coworker that she never actually sent: <br /><br /><i>It is exhausting being me.</i><br /><br />Yes, Jenny, I understand that. I was exhausted just reading your book.<br /><br />At this point I need to clarify, as Jenny often does after she has made an absurd statement, that there are some funny stories here. Jenny had a wackadoo childhood in rural Texas, and her dad liked to drag dead animals home and scare her in the middle of the night. But after about 50 pages I recognized the template of her storytelling, and the repetitiveness of it wore me down. I considered abandoning the book, but so many friends had liked it that I wanted to push through.<br /><br />A few stories are quieter than the rest, such as when her beloved dog died, or when she relates her struggles with anxiety and depression, but there is always an undercurrent of mania. Most of the book is exaggerated fluff, which is fine for a blog, but I don't need it in book form.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14141493240499502498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2034588645810590938">**edited...with content!**<br/><br/>watch your fucking back, sloane crosley...this lady is <i>funny</i>-funny, not "boys tell me i am funny at parties because i am pretty" funny.<br/><br/>i am so glad that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297411747' rel='nofollow noopener'>kelly read this before me</a> and it encouraged me to pick up my ARC and get into it far earlier than i ordinarily would have. BUT NOT EARLIER THAN I WOULD HAVE HAD I ACTUALLY WON THIS THROUGH THE FIRSTREADS PROGRAM, WHICH IS HOW THIS SHOULD HAVE GONE DOWN, GOODREADS!STOP WITH THE SNUBBING ALREADY!<br/><br/>i had never heard of jenny</span>
  <span id="freeText2034588645810590938" style="display:none">**edited...with content!**<br><br>watch your fucking back, sloane crosley...this lady is <i>funny</i>-funny, not "boys tell me i am funny at parties because i am pretty" funny.<br><br>i am so glad that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297411747" rel="nofollow noopener">kelly read this before me</a> and it encouraged me to pick up my ARC and get into it far earlier than i ordinarily would have. BUT NOT EARLIER THAN I WOULD HAVE HAD I ACTUALLY WON THIS THROUGH THE FIRSTREADS PROGRAM, WHICH IS HOW THIS SHOULD HAVE GONE DOWN, GOODREADS!STOP WITH THE SNUBBING ALREADY!<br><br>i had never heard of jenny lawson before, but now i can't stop thinking about her. in a non-creepy way. i think. it's hard for me to gauge my own creepiness when "enthusiastic" can often come across as "creepy." i am pretty sure i am just enthusiastic.<br><br>and it wasn't love at first sight. there were a couple of things in the introduction and first essay that made me wince and hope that some of the "look how hard i am trying!!" missteps would be toned down before publication. i have no way of knowing whether they were. well, i do, but i am lazy. but there were still some genuinely funny moments, and i was on board as she recounted episodes from her childhood with her well-meaning taxidermist father and the...gifts and ...surprises... he would supply for her and her sister. oh, dear. i mean, a lot of the stories sound wonderful and magical like having goats and porcupines and raccoons just hanging out inside the house, wandering around, but for every story featuring a raccoon in jams, there is a story about accidentally running face-first into the carcass of a deer being hosed down in the backyard. and vomiting. inside the carcass of the deer. <br><br>there's no way to come back from that, really. <br><br>i love the fights she has with her long-suffering husband, i love her love of tiny taxidermied animals in period clothing, i love her habit of uncontrollably telling inappropriate stories and lies when cornered at dinner parties, i hate all the deadly things that surround her texas home... except the foxes. greg will like that story.<br><br>i love that i laughed so loud and hard at portions of this book that i had to be checked on because "i thought you were screaming."<br><br>i was totally screaming.<br>and i wet myself a little, too.<br>it was <i>that</i> good.<br><br>i love that she curses as much as i do. and talks about her vagina frequently. in many ways, we are the saaaaaame. we should get a drink together. wait, is that creepy? whatever. <br><br>not a perfect book, no, but a book i liked enough that i am going to buy the hardcover because this ARC has blurry pictures that you can barely read the funny captions on, and the hardcover has these amaaazing patterned endpapers with pictures of animals on them. i love it. and i am waiting for the second book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380377036i/732223._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>call me, jenny. let's taxidermify sloane crosley.<br><br>that was definitely creepy. shit.<br><br><br>okay, so i thought i should give you a sense of her lunacy even though you could just go to her blog and see it, and even though it is totally illegal for me to do so since i only have the ARC, but i am kind of banking on the hope that that is one of those mattress-tag laws and no one will actually come and arrest me, although i would love to see what book prison is like. this isn't one of the passages that made me scream-laugh, but i totally understand her concerns here, and i am frequently startled at the shit we think of.....i like this part mostly because of all the caps and italics and energy jumping off the page....i'll just throw you right into it:<br><br>THIS IS JENNY LAWSON:<br><br><br><br>also, i just want to say that i think when the doctor is stitching your vagina back up (for real, child-free people: <i>stitching. your. vagina. up.</i>), i don't know why they don't throw in some cosmetic surgery while they're down there, to make it look cuter. like, when my gynecologist told me that she'd probably have to cut my vagina, i was all, "YOU ARE A FUCKING PSYCHOPATH," and she was like, "<i>not for fun</i> [unspoken: "<i>dumb-ass"</i>]. to get the baby out." and i said, "oh. well' if you're going to have to scar me, could you do it in some kind of kick-ass shape? like, how about a lightning bolt?" and she just stared at me, so i explained, "you know...like harry potter's?" then she just looked at me like i shit on the floor, and i thought maybe it was because the sentence structure kind of implied i was referring to harry potter's vagina, and so i clarified: "but not on my forehead like his was." and she still didn't respond, so i pointed down and said, "<i>on my vagina</i>" then she shook her head like she'd know all along i wasn't referring to harry potter's vagina, and said, "uh, we don't really do that. in fact, we prefer for you to tear naturally, because it heals better," and i'm all, "MOTHER. FUCKER. are you fucking serious??" and i kind of suspected she was just making that up because she didn't want me to have a nicer vagina than hers, because she's never had a kid and so hers was probably all perfect and cheerful, and she probably didn't want me rubbing my vagina in her face when it was all lightning-bolt awesome. <i>like i would ever even do that, dr. ryder.</i> i would never rub my vagina in someone's face, even though it would be the most badass vagina in the world. and whenever i have menstrual cramps i could just pretend that voldemort was close.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1831924413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13456795007528599291">I read lots of memoirs, but something about Jenny Lawson’s Let’s Pretend this Never Happened was different. REALLY DIFFERENT! It’s not just the messed up lives thing which seems to be a prerequisite for memoir writers. In case you were wondering, though, dysfunctionality thrives in this book. And there is definitely no calm voice of reason beating it back. This dysfunctionality and the bizarre way it manifests energizes Lawson. How Lawson faces this reality, a really skewed and messed up version</span>
  <span id="freeText13456795007528599291" style="display:none">I read lots of memoirs, but something about Jenny Lawson’s Let’s Pretend this Never Happened was different. REALLY DIFFERENT! It’s not just the messed up lives thing which seems to be a prerequisite for memoir writers. In case you were wondering, though, dysfunctionality thrives in this book. And there is definitely no calm voice of reason beating it back. This dysfunctionality and the bizarre way it manifests energizes Lawson. How Lawson faces this reality, a really skewed and messed up version of reality (but probably the one we’re all in denial about) quickly approaches and passes warped! I’ve seen the book described as profanity-laced stream of consciousness, but there are zany and very memorable stories mixed in with her (there’s a squirrel) more distracted moments. It was entertaining to have a glimpse of this world. Good read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13456795007528599291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people with no sense of humour, whiny people, folks with too much spare time Americans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1784452-chris?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1784452-chris?shelf=oh-god-be-merciful-and-kill-me-now">oh-god-be-merciful-and-kill-me-now</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10729230438473426985"><b>Overall Rating: <i>1.5</i></b><br/><br/><br/>I don’t know if it’s specifically American problem, but let me tell you, this is one of the worst memoirs I’ve read. (Seriously America, do you honestly find this <b>funny?</b> O.o) And I’ll tell you why, I’m not just saying this because of some misplaced sense of spite, ok?<br/><br/>When I first heard about this book, I was very excited – it sounded like a real good reading material <i>and</i> it had an awesome cover to boost with too.<br/><br/>From the very beginning though, I realized it would be far from t</span>
  <span id="freeText10729230438473426985" style="display:none"><b>Overall Rating: <i>1.5</i></b><br /><br /><br />I don’t know if it’s specifically American problem, but let me tell you, this is one of the worst memoirs I’ve read. (Seriously America, do you honestly find this <b>funny?</b> O.o) And I’ll tell you why, I’m not just saying this because of some misplaced sense of spite, ok?<br /><br />When I first heard about this book, I was very excited – it sounded like a real good reading material <i>and</i> it had an awesome cover to boost with too.<br /><br />From the very beginning though, I realized it would be far from the book I expected. I have no idea who this individual(Jenny Lawson) is, but the whole book was one big mess, full of stories that were meant to be funny and unique (but were neither). Every single story felt forced and exaggerated. The author couldn’t stop herself from constantly reminding and insisting her childhood was unique and that she’s gone through SO MUCH and so on and so on…<br />Well, be sure it’s not. Maybe for someone living in modern America it’s rarity to have to collect water in a cistern or to have wild animals for pets, etc, etc. But for the rest of the world it’s daily occurrences. The only thing that this book makes me want is to slap the oh, so great nation of “liberty” and shout “<b>GET YOURSELF TOGETHER FOR FUCK’S SAKE! YOU HAVE IT BETTER THAN SO MANY PEOPLE, AND STILL YOU ONLY WHINE!</b>”<br /></span>

<div id="review_2345615234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2345615234" />
    <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus"><img alt="JV (semi-hiatus)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559624981p2/20906165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2345615234?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JV (semi-hiatus)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JV (semi-hiatus)" href="/user/show/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus">JV (semi-hiatus)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=humour-me">humour-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20906165-jv-semi-hiatus?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2345615234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4055513110476320338">Meh. I firmly believe that I might have to re-evaluate and recalibrate my sense of humour after reading this book. Well, humour is rather a subjective one akin to how reviews are also perceived, aye? It was indeed quite difficult for me to rate this memoir as I find it rather grating, hyperbolic, and solipsistic yet hilarious in some spots albeit not quite what I had expected it to be. Lawson has this odd sense of humour which most readers might relate to, but only partially for me, since her wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4055513110476320338" style="display:none">Meh. I firmly believe that I might have to re-evaluate and recalibrate my sense of humour after reading this book. Well, humour is rather a subjective one akin to how reviews are also perceived, aye? It was indeed quite difficult for me to rate this memoir as I find it rather grating, hyperbolic, and solipsistic yet hilarious in some spots albeit not quite what I had expected it to be. Lawson has this odd sense of humour which most readers might relate to, but only partially for me, since her wavelength definitely didn't coincide with mine. <br /><br />The laugh-out-loud moments are distributed sparsely. However, most parts of this memoir didn't trigger the guffaw factor that I would get from reading and enjoying a Peanuts comic strip or watching shows or movies like in the <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt2802144" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Kingsman: The Secret Service</a> as well as other favourites which I definitely adore namely Mr. Bean (both the <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0096657" rel="nofollow noopener">original</a> and <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0280277" rel="nofollow noopener">animated</a> one), <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0100366" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pingu</a>, <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0220880" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Courage The Cowardly Dog</a>, <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0242213" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Lulu Show</a>, <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0115157" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dexter's Laboratory</a> (especially the Omelette du Fromage story), and <a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt1845307" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">2 Broke Girls</a> to name a few! Honestly, this memoir didn't blew my socks off but there are, surely, parts that are worthy to be remembered for its golden nugget of wisdom:<blockquote>
  <i>"Because I can finally see that all the terrible parts of my life, the embarrassing parts, the incidents I wanted to pretend never happened, and the things that make me “weird” and “different,” were actually the most important parts of my life. They were the parts that made me me. And this was the very reason I decided to tell this story . . . to celebrate the strange, to give thanks for the bizarre [...] Because you are defined not by life’s imperfect moments, but by your reaction to them. Because there is joy in embracing—rather than running screaming from — the utter absurdity of life."</i>
</blockquote>Despite the random ruminations and seemingly coerced humour, it's neither a bad nor great read either, but I do find it to be as dull as a ditchwater and it's just bloody me! So, folks, we have to agree to disagree! Note that there are hilarious moments to wit: <br /><br />(1) Rambo the racoon; hobos and Daffodil the duck (poor duck); (2) having a sex concussion; (3) artificially inseminating a cow with turkey baster; (4) HR stories: résumé showing that someone worked at "Helping Hand-Jobs" and asking employees about "Is this your penis?"; (5) yoga farting; (6) extra-strength laxative vs. the Pepto-Bismol; (7) chasing vultures away with a machete.<br /><br />By the way, before you pick up the audiobook version, think again! Just 10 minutes in and I already gave up! Why? Because the author sounded like a hormonal, cutesy, high-school teenager with way over-the-top performance. As my final PSA, I would rather happily grate my favourite cheese on a six-pack or eight-pack abdominals of a smokin' hot guy basking in the sun rather than grate my auditory canals and further subject myself to the author's nerve-racking voice. Now if you'll excuse me, I might need to get in touch with my otorhinolaryngologist for a comprehensive examination of my ears for I dread the fact that that ten-minute audiobook immersion alone was enough for my auditory system to go haywire further resulting to my eardrums getting perforated! <br /><br />Let's just pretend I've never read this, but well, it did happen. Sheesh! A vacillating 2 to 3 stars, but will settle for a 2! <br /><br /><b><a href="https://www.audible.com/pd/Lets-Pretend-This-Never-Happened-Audiobook/B007T7U0RK" rel="nofollow noopener">Audiobook</a> rating (narrated by Jenny Lawson):</b><br />Narrative voice &amp; style - ★★<br />Vocal characterisation - ★<br />Inflexion &amp; intonation - ★<br />Voice quality - ★½<br /><b>Audiobook verdict</b> - ★ (Don't bother!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4055513110476320338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15315559927222614817">Basically the best review I can give this book, is that as a librarian I'm pretty much giddy with excitement waiting for the things people will come tell me after they've read this book. From the (boring) I loved that it was an honest look at mental illness and survival (very true) to the (no seriously I can not wait) YOU LET MY CHILD READ THIS AND NOW THEY WANT A DEAD SQUIRREL PUPPET and THIS BOOK IS BLASPHEMY AND READING IT KILLS PUPPIES AND KITTENS.<br/><br/>I pretty much giggled in excitement when I w</span>
  <span id="freeText15315559927222614817" style="display:none">Basically the best review I can give this book, is that as a librarian I'm pretty much giddy with excitement waiting for the things people will come tell me after they've read this book. From the (boring) I loved that it was an honest look at mental illness and survival (very true) to the (no seriously I can not wait) YOU LET MY CHILD READ THIS AND NOW THEY WANT A DEAD SQUIRREL PUPPET and THIS BOOK IS BLASPHEMY AND READING IT KILLS PUPPIES AND KITTENS.<br /><br />I pretty much giggled in excitement when I won the advance copy, and then waited not really patiently to get my copy and then it came and I was away and that basically destroyed me and there was a 3 day long emotional trauma period. Anyways. I finally got to my copy and it was everything I wanted it to be. Heart-breakingly (also, it tries to auto-correct breakingly to lawbreaking. Fitting) wonderful, actually laugh out loud funny (not just LOL'd) and hands down one of my favourite memoirs and books out there. <br /><br />Go. Buy it. As soon as you can. I might buy it again so I can see the pictures. But then, I kind of loved that they were blurry. But I'm weird. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vivalakt.blogspot.ca/">http://vivalakt.blogspot.ca/</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer331743257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11345471065018657842"><br/>Jenny Lawson (aka <a href='http://thebloggess.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bloggess</a>) is seriously effed up, and that doesn't always equate with being seriously bleeping funny but in her case, this book will S-L-A-Y you. I laughed so hard in parts I shed tears (and a little pee I think). Just sayin'. For anyone out there with some incontinence issues already. <br/><br/>Her frantic, stream-of-consciousness delivery (though punctuated with gems of insane hilarity) can get exhausting. Sometimes you just want to scream, "Jenny, will you just shut the *&%@# up al</span>
  <span id="freeText11345471065018657842" style="display:none"><br />Jenny Lawson (aka <a href="http://thebloggess.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bloggess</a>) is seriously effed up, and that doesn't always equate with being seriously bleeping funny but in her case, this book will S-L-A-Y you. I laughed so hard in parts I shed tears (and a little pee I think). Just sayin'. For anyone out there with some incontinence issues already. <br /><br />Her frantic, stream-of-consciousness delivery (though punctuated with gems of insane hilarity) can get exhausting. Sometimes you just want to scream, "Jenny, will you just shut the *&amp;%@# up already!" -- imagine being stuck in an elevator with a coked up Robin Williams who just also happens to be sipping on a Red Bull laced with vodka. As horrible as <i>that</i> sounds, Jenny Lawson makes it work. Despite her frantic crazy energy, she <i>will</i> make you laugh your ass off, teach you how to curse like a sailor (that woman loves to let the expletives fly), force you to appreciate all of life's absurdities, face tragedy with (enough) dignity, and be grateful for every single blessing that you have. <br /><br />She also taught me that the most interesting person in the room is probably the one hiding under the table (or in the bathroom) hyperventilating. Only stupid people aren't locked and loaded for the zombie apocalypse (well d'uh, that one I knew already). That chupacabras are REAL. That people who tell you that acupuncture is painless are "complete fucking liars." And most important of all, Texas may be big and beautiful and have awesome BBQ, but it's also where all the bitey, stinging things live. <blockquote>Today the exterminator came out to spray for scorpions <i>again</i>, and he left a note saying that he found an enormous snakeskin next to our house. Then I screamed, "EVERYTHING IN THE COUNTRY WANTS TO KILL YOU," and Victor told me to go lie down. But then I went to look at the snakeskin, and I was all, "This is a used paper towel." Then Victor said, "Dude. That's totally a snakeskin that's been shed. Look at the diamond scale pattern," and I was all, "That's a textured diamond weave to absorb more wetness. You can tell it's a paper towel because snakeskins aren't square. Or perforated." And I spread it out on the ground and then he was all, "Huh. That is a fucking paper towel. I think we need a new exterminator." We're probably not going to survive the year.</blockquote><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11345471065018657842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11137631765568001039"><b>WINNER - Goodreads Choice Awards, Best Humor 2012</b><br/><br/>Wonderfully unconventional and refreshing! Jenny Lawson shares stories of growing up in rural Texas, with a loving (albeit overly-enthusiastic) taxidermist for a father and a sister who grinned and bore it with her. Lawson writes about meeting her husband for the first time and seeing his confused looks as he becomes more and more familiar with the idiosyncrasies of her colorful family.<br/><br/>She also shares her debilitating social anxiety, recounting fu</span>
  <span id="freeText11137631765568001039" style="display:none"><b>WINNER - Goodreads Choice Awards, Best Humor 2012</b><br /><br />Wonderfully unconventional and refreshing! Jenny Lawson shares stories of growing up in rural Texas, with a loving (albeit overly-enthusiastic) taxidermist for a father and a sister who grinned and bore it with her. Lawson writes about meeting her husband for the first time and seeing his confused looks as he becomes more and more familiar with the idiosyncrasies of her colorful family.<br /><br />She also shares her debilitating social anxiety, recounting funny "awkward moment" stories from parties and social situations. They're hilarious but also touching.<br /><br />I suspect Lawson has always turned to comedy as a way to help alleviate her suffering... and all that practice has perfected her gift. This girl is FUNNY. More than that, this memoir makes you feel that all those little supposed 'weird' things that make you 'you' are really okay, awesome actually, and should be treasured.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/319254105?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Guzman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Guzman" href="/user/show/4014423-maria-guzman">Maria Guzman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer319254105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3628318689715916235">I think there might be something wrong with my sense of humor. I tried to read this book but it's not making me laugh. In fact, it's making me annoyed. It reminds me of a whiny nagger who is all about "me". Oh right, it's a memoir. Anyway, I jumped to some of the chapters to see if I missed anything funny but it was all the same. I'm giving away my copy in the hope that someone may find it funny and not completely waste the tree that this book was printed on. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1468192862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1468192862" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1468192862?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1468192862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10511523793691144902"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle deal 16May20 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Lets-Pretend-This-Never-Happened-ebook/dp/B0065S8R38/ref=sr_1_143?dchild=1&qid=1589637593&s=digital-text&sr=1-143' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99</a><b><br/><br/><b>Pandemic Recommendation</b> I forgot how much fun I had with this book. If you are in need of some laughs and lighthearted moments this might be just perfect right now.<br/><br/><b>4.5 I Laughed So Hard I Peed a Little Stars</b><br/><br/>Buddy read with some of my friends at <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b> because after I read <a>Beyonce the Chicken</a> there was no way I was not going to read her book.<br/><br/>Humor is a really subjective thing. Either something falls into stuff you think is funny or it doesn’</b></b></span>
  <span id="freeText10511523793691144902" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle deal 16May20 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Lets-Pretend-This-Never-Happened-ebook/dp/B0065S8R38/ref=sr_1_143?dchild=1&amp;qid=1589637593&amp;s=digital-text&amp;sr=1-143" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99</a><b><br /><br /><b>Pandemic Recommendation</b> I forgot how much fun I had with this book. If you are in need of some laughs and lighthearted moments this might be just perfect right now.<br /><br /><b>4.5 I Laughed So Hard I Peed a Little Stars</b><br /><br />Buddy read with some of my friends at <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b> because after I read <a>Beyonce the Chicken</a> there was no way I was not going to read her book.<br /><br />Humor is a really subjective thing. Either something falls into stuff you think is funny or it doesn’t. Regretfully my hubs LOVEs Jackass type humor and all Will Ferrell movies. But for me that stuff is hit and miss. Either I love it or I roll my eyes at the ridiculousness of the entire thing. Jenny Lawson is <b>MY KIND OF FUNNY</b> and I had the best time in her book.<br /><br />But is she going to be your kind of funny??? She will not be for everyone, so ask yourself these important questions:<br /><br />① - Do you like to laugh? <i>I totally love to laugh…I try to laugh at myself and others as much as possible.</i><br /><br />② - Are you okay with some vulgar language like the use of f-bombs? <i>It is totally okay with me. My motto is <b>you can say it if it is funny.</b></i><br /><br />③ - Are you comfortable with references to vaginas? <i>I have a Ronald Reagan (you’ll get that if you listened to the audiobook) and I know what they do so again reference my answer to #2.</i><br /><br />④ - Do you like humorous personal stories where some unexpected things happen, like a bobcat being thrown on you or a serial killer on the other side of the bathroom door tries to pass you a note? <i>Well I do enjoy a good story with a serial killer in it and who doesn’t think an unexpected bobcat being thrown in someone’s lap is hilarious???</i><br /><br />⑤ - Do you like reading/listening to others peoples messed up lives that make you realize that “no, you are not that crazy or fucked up and by comparison you are the pinnacle of sanity”? <i>YES, I love stories that make me laugh and realize that <b>no matter what crazy things I’ve said or done I have never had my arm stuck in a cow vagina</b> and therefor really life isn’t that bad.</i><br /><blockquote><i> “no matter how shitty it got, I could always look back and say, “At least I don’t have my arm stuck up a cow’s vagina.” In fact, that’s kind of become my life’s motto. It’s also what I say when I’m at a loss for words when talking to people who are grieving the loss of their grandparents.”</i></blockquote><br />But seriously while some of the stories were semi-serious with a big dose of funny mixed in most of the chapters and stories where just down right laugh-out-loud funny <br /><br /><b>Dear Victor:</b><br /><br />I wanted to feel sorry for you sometimes while reading this because that your wife can seem to go off the deep end. But then I thought about and realized that for all the crazy panic attacky/or inappropriate things that come out of her mouth she really must be incredibly fun to have in a day to day world and she probably keeps you on your toes. <br /><br />A few of my favorite moments from the book were the conversations you had together even if they were bickering or bantering they seemed mostly playful and fun. That said I side with Jenny on the Snake, the Metal Chicken and Couch Etiquette (who knew there was such a thing) but I’ll totally side with you on housework, the GPS and zombies. <br /><br />P.S. - I think Jenny’s first book is so much fun I plan to listen to it with my husband on our next road trip.<br /><br />P.P.S - If you can get both the print edition because it has some super funny pictures and the audio since Jenny is so funny while she reads her own book. But really if you chose just one I HIGHLY recommend the audio.<br /><br />P.P.P.S – Here are a few quotes from inside the book. Because seriously had I read some of these I probably would have read her book sooner. Or at least followed her blog.<br /><blockquote><b>Family dynamics</b><br /><br /><i> “The Dangerous Thesaurus of My Father.” An abridged version:<br /> “It’s very excited.” = “It has rabies.” <br />“Now, don’t get too attached.” = “I got this monkey for free because it has a virus.” <br />“Now, this is really interesting.” = “You’ll still have nightmares about this when you’re thirty.”</i><br /><br /><b>High School Embarrassing Moments</b><br /><br /><i>"And that’s how I ended up shoulder-deep in a cow’s vagina, squishing out the semen baster as a bunch of teenage boys looked on. It was the closest I’d ever come to doing porn. </i><br /><br /><b>Falling in Love</b><br /><br /> <i>"I wanted to cheer him up, but it felt weird wanting to cheer up someone who was possibly depressed because they didn’t murder you correctly, and that’s when I thought, “This must be what love is. When you want to make it less difficult for someone to murder you.” And that’s when I realized that I was far too in love with him for my own good, and also that I probably needed therapy</i><br /><br /><b>Having a Baby</b><br /><br /><i>"Like, when my gynecologist told me that she’d probably have to cut my vagina, I was all, “YOU ARE A FUCKING PSYCHOPATH,” and she was like, “Not for fun [unspoken: “dumb-ass”]. To get the baby out.” And I said, “Oh. Well, if you’re going to have to scar me, could you do it in some kind of kick-ass shape? Like, how about a lightning bolt?”</i><br /><br /><b>Meeting New People</b><br /><br /><i>“I've found, though, that people are more likely to share their personal experiences if you go first, so that's why I always keep an eleven-point list of what went wrong in my childhood to share with them. Also I usually crack open a bottle of tequila to share with them, because alcohol makes me less nervous, and also because I'm from the South, and in Texas we offer drinks to strangers even when we're waiting in line at the liquor store. In Texas we call that '_southern hospitality_.' The people who own the liquor store call it 'shoplifting.' Probably because they're Yankees.<br />I'm not allowed to go back to that liquor store.”</i><br /><br /><b>Jenny’s Vagina</b><br /><br /><i>“...I just want to clarify that I don't mean 'without my vagina' like I didn't have it with me at the time. I just mean that I wasn't, you know...displaying it while I was at Starbucks. That's probably understood, but I thought I should clarify, since it's the first chapter and you don't know that much about me. So just to clarify, I always have my vagina with me. It's like my American Express card. (In that I don't leave home without it. Not that I use it to buy stuff with.)”</i></blockquote><br /><b>Overall</b> - If you just need a good time and a good laugh than save this for then. There were so many wonderful moments in this and I loved the time I spent with Jenny and her myriad or misadventures and life’s learning experiences. I laughed so hard in some spots I might have peed a little.</b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10511523793691144902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Josie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/360518-josie"><img alt="Josie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204659361p2/360518.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/342776244?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Josie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Josie" href="/user/show/360518-josie">Josie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611760859" href="/book/show/12844430-let-s-pretend-this-never-happened">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer342776244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6702651032508144375">When Jenny Lawson relates a childhood story she's funny and engaging...but so far, that's only occurred for about 10% of her writing in this book. The other 90% I've read is just terrible. The parenthetical ramblings and anxious Turrets-style outbursts quickly get old, and they distract from some of the really funny and entertaining bits. Everything is "totally" or "basically" life-threatening or she's stabbing or kicking someone in the balls "in her head." Her nervous, panicky breakdowns feel l</span>
  <span id="freeText6702651032508144375" style="display:none">When Jenny Lawson relates a childhood story she's funny and engaging...but so far, that's only occurred for about 10% of her writing in this book. The other 90% I've read is just terrible. The parenthetical ramblings and anxious Turrets-style outbursts quickly get old, and they distract from some of the really funny and entertaining bits. Everything is "totally" or "basically" life-threatening or she's stabbing or kicking someone in the balls "in her head." Her nervous, panicky breakdowns feel like an act -- an act that has gotten her laughs in the past, so she leans on it rather than exploring her more genuine writing talents. Her constant arguments with her husband are particularly tiresome -- they're like that one couple everyone knows who like to argue in front of other people, playing up the theatrics of their exasperating roles. I'm 70% through the Kindle version, and I don't think I can continue. But, I'm giving two stars because, hidden in the muck, there are a few gems here. This is one in a slew of recent books that many friends have rated highly, where I'm left clueless after reading. Is it me? </span>
  <a data-text-id="6702651032508144375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_528684581" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528684581" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/528684581?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611760859" href="/book/show/12844430-let-s-pretend-this-never-happened">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who love odd humor and can tolerate swearing</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      while it was on my to-read, I confess Trudi's description made me bump it up
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=auto-biography">auto-biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=female-lead">female-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer528684581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16124758382081317092"><br/>Oh, Jenny.<br/><br/>There is something so completely...<br/><br/>extravagant  [ik-strav-uh-guhnt]<br/>Part of Speech: 	adjective<br/>Definition: 	exceeding the bounds of reason, as actions, demands, opinions, or passions. <br/>Synonyms: 	absurd, bizarre, crazy, exaggerated, excessive, exorbitant, extreme, fanciful, fantastic, flamboyant, flashy, foolish, grandiose, immoderate, implausible, improvident, imprudent, inordinate, lavish, ludicrous, nonsensical, ornate, outrageous, preposterous, pretentious, prodigal, profligate, reckl</span>
  <span id="freeText16124758382081317092" style="display:none"><br />Oh, Jenny.<br /><br />There is something so completely...<br /><br />extravagant  [ik-strav-uh-guhnt]<br />Part of Speech: 	adjective<br />Definition: 	exceeding the bounds of reason, as actions, demands, opinions, or passions. <br />Synonyms: 	absurd, bizarre, crazy, exaggerated, excessive, exorbitant, extreme, fanciful, fantastic, flamboyant, flashy, foolish, grandiose, immoderate, implausible, improvident, imprudent, inordinate, lavish, ludicrous, nonsensical, ornate, outrageous, preposterous, pretentious, prodigal, profligate, reckless, ridiculous, showy, silly, unbalanced, unrestrained.<br /><br />about this (mostly true) memoir.<br /><br />That about sums it up.<br /><br />******************************************************<br />Notes on the audiobook:<br /><br /><b>One,</b> it's rather adorable, as she is the reader. Her attempting to verbally describe pictures and footnotes that would be in the book version cracked me up, leaving me wondering if I should read the written book just to compare. <br /><br /><b>Two,</b> Jenny shines at non-sequitur chains of ideas, at capturing a conversational tone in her writing, and at appreciating oddity. For me, she is at her best when capturing a 'funny-but-odd' situation, segueing into nutty metaphors and bringing it back to the odd situation. A perfect example is her description of a childhood horror that resulted from her father cleaning a deer. She amusingly sets the scene, then tangents off on an aside for "sensitive PETA members" on what "cleaning a deer" means:<br /><br />"You get some warm water, and some tearless shampoo, and you gently massage the deer. Lather, rinse, but don't repeat even though the bottle says to, because that's just a ploy to sell more shampoo, blow dry on low heat and hot-glue a bow on his forehead. Send him back into the woods to meet a nice Jewish doe. Go to the next chapter." <br /><br />She then shares what <i>really</i> cleaning a deer means for "curious, non-judgmental readers"--and it apparently involves the "poop rope," the first time I've been privileged to hear that "French" expression despite having a deer hunter father as well. Once that is finished she returns to the truly horrible experience of running into the hanging carcass. And throwing up. And her father's version of the "Grizzly Adams five-second rule."<br /><br />Likewise, "bonus" chapter titled "Balls" was a delight, and perfectly captures oddball humor and the even odder people around her. She balances the laughs created by her naivate, the ridiculous extrapolation of a situation (think tongue-on-ice and short-shorts) and compassionate (their vengeful Sno-cone fund-raiser).<br /><br /><b>Two-point-five:</b>: It doesn't happen often, but occasionally there are sound effects accompanying the audio. The knife sharpening in the deer section was a sinister touch. <br /><b>Two-point-seven-five:</b> She sings the chapter titles. It is truly an ear-cringing experience.<br /><br /><b>Three,</b> I suggest numerous listening/reading breaks. She is overwhelming, particularly in the section of the book that deals with her relationships. Funny as hell, but listen too long and I run the risk of diminishing returns from sheer exhaustion.<br /><br /><b>Four</b>--and this may be just me--but I found myself melancholic at times, particularly the chapter about the women bloggers' weekend, the section on her 'detoxification by laxatives,' the post-it exchanges with Victor, and the dog burial. Mental illness runs through the book and is rarely discussed openly, except in the chapter that she talks about her social anxiety, general anxiety disorder and panic attacks. There's a whole lot of sadness left out of a story about a miscarriage, and from her abridged explanation, a whole lot of crazy. <br /><br />The crazy is almost always played for laughs, and while I get smiling through the pain, appreciating uniqueness, holding one's head high, making lemonade, sharing the pain, etc., etc., I just don't know. It was a thin line that sometimes felt closer to laughing at someone with cancer than with them. (No, no one in the book had cancer. That's just my metaphorical way of saying laughing at mental illness' oddities is a lot like laughing at someone struggling with cancer. It can be all-consuming, can come endowed with lots of symptom baggage and can be a constant struggle. And they probably had about as much choice in the matter. So even if they play the clumps of hair falling out for laughs--and many people do--it still represents a whole lot of hurt behind the smile. And, now that I think about it, there is that same sense of trying to conceal the horror as I watch it happen).<br /><br /><b>Five,</b> for her sake and the sake of the millions living with mental health issues--because don't fool yourself, most people have a fissure that just takes the right experience to break it open--I hope she claims some political power and doesn't just settle for laughs.<br /><br />A wavering three-and-a-half stars.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/03/17/lets-pretend-this-never-happened-by-jenny-lawson-or-laughing-on-the-outside/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2013/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16124758382081317092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_276925941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276925941" />
    <a title="Jaime Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1837527-jaime-brown"><img alt="Jaime Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303509633p2/1837527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276925941?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Brown" href="/user/show/1837527-jaime-brown">Jaime Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781611760859" href="/book/show/12844430-let-s-pretend-this-never-happened">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276925941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13259551032831072375">I’m not sure what I enjoyed more about this book. The actual laughing to tears moments while reading or the actual laughing to tears moments while retelling the stories to my boyfriend (who kept mentioning that he and Victor have a lot in common). <br/><br/>It says a great deal about Jenny Lawson (of blogging fame) that at 38, she was able to write a 300+ page memoir that is interesting to read. Interesting, not because she is a celebrity or has boinked a celebrity, but because she has lived a strange lif</span>
  <span id="freeText13259551032831072375" style="display:none">I’m not sure what I enjoyed more about this book. The actual laughing to tears moments while reading or the actual laughing to tears moments while retelling the stories to my boyfriend (who kept mentioning that he and Victor have a lot in common). <br /><br />It says a great deal about Jenny Lawson (of blogging fame) that at 38, she was able to write a 300+ page memoir that is interesting to read. Interesting, not because she is a celebrity or has boinked a celebrity, but because she has lived a strange life and has maintained a good attitude about that life. As Lawson mentions in her prologue, “you are defined, not by life’s imperfect moments, but by your reaction to them.” This sets the tone for the book. Lawson could have written a book about her parent’s questionable child-rearing skills. She could have written a book about tearful issues with fertility. Instead, Lawson wrote a story that holds dark aspects but is told in a lighthearted manner. <br /><br />Lawson is able to play the role of an unreliable narrator with grace. I’m not sure whether she truly believes in what she says or if she says she believes as such for laughs. Either way, it works for me. <br /><br />My only disappointment was at the end of the book, when I had turned the last page. I did not want this trip into the mind of Lawson to be over, I wanted to stay in her world for just a bit more. <br /><br />Luck for us, Lawson blogs about her life so that we can have a taste to keep us happy until her next book. <br /><br />I would recommend this book … to people with a dark sense of humor who do not mind stories coming from a lady with the mouth of a trucker. Well, if a trucker and a sailor had a baby, that baby would be Jenny Lawson. <br /><br />My favorite quote … “My God, this is going to be a terrible book.”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13259551032831072375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
